After I have completed for you, O my sons, this book, which is the last of the science of medicine with its completion, and I have reached the end of it, from its expositions and its explanations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Because the operation with the hand is prostrate in our region and in our time, completely deprived, until perhaps its science perished, and its trace was cut off: and there remained from it only small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have changed: and error and hesitation happened to them, until its intentions were closed, and its force was removed: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way of exposition, and explanation, and abbreviation: and that I should come with the forms of the instruments of cautery, and the other instruments of the work: when it is done by the addition of explanation, and by the hastening of what is necessary.
The reason, however, why a good craftsman with his hand is not found in this our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be exercised before it in the science of anatomy, which Galen has narrated, until he knows the aids of the limbs, and their forms, and their connection, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and muscles, and their number, and their course, and of pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their exit.
And because of that Hippocrates said that the name is much with the name, and little with the work, and especially in the art of the hand.
We indeed already said about that in the introduction of this book.
Because he who is not knowing what we said about anatomy is not emptied, but already falls into error, by which men are killed: just as I saw many of those who are formed in this science, and boast of it without knowledge and without experiment.
That is, because I saw a foolish physician cut an scrofulous abscess in the neck of a woman, and he cut certain arteries in the neck: wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man who was advanced in age, and the stone was large. Therefore he arrived at it, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone, and the disposition of the sick man, that he would die.
And I saw another physician who received a stipend from a certain Duke of our land on account of medicine: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture above the wound with cushions and splints with a strong binding, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he cured him according to his desires. Afterwards he dismissed him after several days, and ordered him not to loosen the bandage: and it remained so until his leg and his foot became suppurated, and came to ruin.
Therefore I was called to him: and I hastened to loosen the bandage: and calmness followed, and he escaped from his pains.
Nevertheless, the corruption was already established in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore the corruption ceased to spread in the limb, until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who perforated a cancerous abscess: and it ulcerated afterwards, until its malignancy was magnified with its master.
That is, because when a cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to approach it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb which can tolerate having the whole of it cut off.
And for that reason, O my son, it is necessary for you to know that manual operation is divided into two divisions: namely, operation associated with safety: and operation with which there is danger in many conditions.
And I have already pointed out in every place in this book where an operation occurs which involves terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to avoid it and leave it alone, so that fools may not find a way to speak of it and bring dishonor.
Therefore take measures with care and protection, and treat your patients with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to salvation and laudable success: and leave alone terrible illnesses of difficult healing: and remove your minds from that which makes you afraid, lest hesitation enter into your faith and your well-being.
For it is more conducive to your glory, and more exalted in this world, and finally to your rewards.
For Galen already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness: lest you be called bad physicians.
Now however I have divided this treatise according to three chapters.
Chapter one.
Concerning cautery with fire, and cautery with a sharp medicine, chaptered and ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments, and the tools of cautery: and everything which is necessary in the operation.
Chapter two.
Concerning incision and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to that: and the whole chaptered, ordered with forms of instruments.
Chapter three.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of torsion, and similar things: chaptered, ordered from head to foot, and with forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its helps and harms: and in what complexion it should be exhibited.
Therefore I say that the discourse concerning the quality of the help of cautery, and its harm, is a lengthy and subtle discourse, a science, and a hidden secret.
Many wise men have also spoken on it, and they have disagreed: and indeed a little from their sayings suffices me, fearing prolixity.
Therefore I say that cautery benefits universally every complexion which is with matter and without matter, except for two complexions, which are a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
However, in a hot and dry complexion with matter they disagreed. For some have said that cautery is helpful in it. And others said the contrary of that, namely that cautery is not suitable in the illness which is from heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable that a hot and dry illness should be healed with something hot and dry.
And he who says the contrary of that said: that through cautery help is given in every hot and dry illness which happens in the bodies of men: because when you compare the body of man and its humors to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I indeed say through his account: because experience has already revealed that to me several times.
Nevertheless it is not fitting that he come to that, except he who is already proven and practiced in the chapter of cautery, in the final exercise, and has known the diversity of the complexions of men, and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their duration.
From the other complexions however there is no fear for you: and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For already all physicians have agreed upon them: and they did not disagree in helping with cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of treatment by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine is: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined with it, except with little harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from the members: and perhaps it causes illness difficult to heal in a member, and perhaps it kills.
Fire however, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now indeed that has become known to us through experiment, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing upon the truth of things: and because of that I excuse myself from lengthy speech.
And if it were not that it is not permitted in this my book, I would bring to you a hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with a philosophical demonstrative speech, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree in the time in which it is fitting to perform cautery, and they place the better time in spring.
And I say that cautery is fitting at all times: because the harm occurring because of time is submerged in the benefit which is attracted with cautery. And especially if cautery is because of pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains which do not tolerate slowness: because it is feared from them that a greater harm might occur than the small harm entering because of time.
And let not that fall into your minds, O sons, which only the common people and foolish physicians fear, namely that that illness which is healed by cautery does not always return: and they posit this as a consequence, and the matter is not as they think: because cautery is nothing but a medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humors which are the causes why pains occur.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in the speed of its health, and the strength of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the illness may return at some time according to the complexion of the infirm, and the location of his illness, and its strength: and that which is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it: and that which arrives at it in its acquisition from foods, and similar causes, unless the illness in which cautery is administered occurs.
An illness subtle in a member of few superfluities and humors, such as cautery of a tooth because of pain, and similar things, for it is possible that that pain may not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But truly the speech of the common people again, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is a right speech: not to that which they intend in it: for they believe that there is no cure which confers with medicine, nor with anything else after the application of cautery.
The matter, however, is contrary to that, and the intention that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not so, except when we administer methods of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not help: then we administer cautery at the end of the matter, and it helps: then it follows that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients, however, said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron: and they did not say that, except because of the evenness of gold and the excellence of its substance: and they said that the place of cautery does not produce pus. But that is not true absolutely: because I have now proven that, and I have found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat a cautery in the fire made of gold, it is not clear to you when it is heated to the desired amount, because of the redness of the gold; and when it approaches cold, and if you add more heating to it, it melts in the fire and turns into flakes.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into difficulty with it: and because of that, cautery with iron is quicker and more convenient for us, because of its suitability for the operation.
And I have indeed arranged this chapter on cautery according to chapters: and I have arranged them from head to foot: so that they may alleviate for the one seeking what he wants from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization contributes to the control of moisture and coldness over the brain: which two are causes of headache, and an abundance of the flow of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain: and universally every illness which happens from coldness, such as paralysis, and headache, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the patient: that he be purged first with a cleansing resolvent medicine for three or four nights, according to what the strength of the patient, and his age, and his habit require.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit squarely between your hands, so that he now places his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that place with ink.
Then heat the olive cautery; its form is this.
Then place it on the place marked with ink, descending, so that your hand is gradually tightened, and you will roll it. Then quickly lift your hand, and look at the place.
If you see now revealed from the bone the amount of the head of alkiel, or the amount of zeuherbi, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat with your hand the same iron, or with another like it if it cools; until you see the bones which I told you about.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cautery in it, and place it on the place: and leave it for three days.
Then place on it the cautery soaked in butter, and leave it on the place, until the fire scab is destroyed. Then treat it with tetrapharmacon ointment, until it is healed.
They have said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits: wherefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized to the bone: and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of the bone is burned.
Then shave off what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the end with the cautery, until it makes a strong impression on the bone, so that the bone falls, which is made like the shape of a kirate: or an instrument that women put in the infusion of small letters: and they think that vapors from the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it consolidates.
But to me these two types of cautery do not seem at all suitable except in certain men, according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for its health.
For the head is weakened by the separation of its natural continuity, as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head of the sick person is naturally weak: and indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore operate with it safely.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs in the whole head and it is prolonged in the sick person, and he uses bleedings, and potions, and head purges, and oils, and cataplasms. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and none of those things benefit him: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and is not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery a little below it. Then cauterize it above every horn of his head with a cautery, until the skin is not pierced, and a quantity of bone, which we have described, is uncovered. And cauterize it with one cautery in the occiput of his head, in the place which is called a vessel: and it is the place where a cupping glass is placed: and raise your instrument in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the sick person finds because of that a very intense pain, and different from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And I shall call this cauterization in its place: and it is necessary that it be a cauterization, by which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its occiput with a finer cautery, by which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is evacuated with cleansing medicines, and the remaining treatment, which I mentioned in the divisions of illnesses, is administered, and it does not entirely help: then cauterization is used in it according to two methods: either cauterization with a sharp burning medicine: or with iron.
Now, cauterization with a sharp burning medicine is as follows: take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends on both sides. Then incise the painful area at the time with a broad phlebotomy knife, until a space is made under the skin in which the clove is placed.
Then insert it under the skin until it is hidden: then bind over it with a suitable compress, and leave it for fifteen hours; then unbind it, and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days: afterwards apply a piece of cloth soaked in butter to it, until the place produces pus: then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do it with some burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, on burning medicines.
Cauterization with an iron, however, is in this manner. A fire cautery, whose shape is this.
And it is called a nail, because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it there is a small projection.
Then place it on the place, and hold your hand: and you slowly revolve the iron with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be of the thickness of the skin, as much as half of it. And lift your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood happens.
Then soak a pledget in salt water, and place it on the place, and leave it for three days: then place the pledget with butter: afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second knife-like extremity of the Cautery. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not properly an old one.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an old hemicrania.
When you treat a hemicrania with what we have said in the preceding treatment, and what we said in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment does not help: and you see from the illness that what we said about the first cautery with medicine, or with fire cautery, is not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the knife-like cautery until it turns white after you mark on the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or about that: and place your hand in one position, and press it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves in mastication, lest the side be burned, or the nerve which moves it, from which a spasm may result.
And be watchful and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery which has been cut. For in its incision there is danger, and especially to him who is ignorant of what he does, and is not studious, nor experienced: and he leaves the operation with that in the first instance.
And I will come with a recollection of the regime of the flow of blood happening from the artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
But if you see from the sickness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in earache.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and it is treated with resolvents and the other treatment which we mentioned in the division, and the pain is not removed, then cauterize with fire: and it is that which is called a point, whose form is this.
Then make points with it after its ignition around the whole ear, as it is rolled around; or around both, if pain is in both at the same time. And move the cautery away from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with the cautery; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points in each ear, and about that.
Then treat the places until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a twisted [or contorted] condition.
Chapter VII.
The twisted condition which is treated with cauterization is only from the species which happen from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the species which happens from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this species of twisted condition with bleedings, and purgations of the head, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its temple, and a third at the conjunction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected part. Because softening does not happen except in the part which appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the end of the upper ear under the horn of the head a little: and another in the temple: whose length is according to the length of a thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a kind of knife, whose form has been described: however, it is not a little thinner than that, as you see: and it is necessary that there be a little superfluous thickness in the knife.
Then treat the place with what preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes chronic, and you treat it with what we have said, and your treatment does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cautery in the occiput of the head, according to what preceded: and the method of cauterization should be according to what preceded.
Also, cauterization is done with a cautery over the stomach; and this is more extreme.
Then let him be treated with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that at first, great hiera and pills purifying the brain be given to the sick person in a drink.
Then shave the whole head of the sick person, and place upon his occiput a plaster of mustard described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it several times.
For this is the method of cauterization: and do it according to the same order which I described there.
Therefore if he is healed by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauterizations in the posterior part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cauterization the width of a finger.
Then take care of the cauterization, with that which preceded.
But if you wish an addition, and the patient is able to tolerate it: then make for him a cauterization in the middle. But if you wish an addition: then cauterize it above the two horns.
Then treat it until it heals: and let the cauterization be olive-shaped according to the form which was described before.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in the cleansing of the head with hyssop, and with that which we said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery above each horn of the head, and with a cautery behind it, and with three above the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you need in the sickness a softening of the body with more of those things, and the infirm person is tolerant, and the sickness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauteries above the vertebrae of the back, and finally with a cautery, until much of his skin is burned, and raise your hand. Then take care of him until he is healed: and thus cauterize Oliuare.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, except one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with herbs, and with the other treatment which we have described in the division: when the patient is strong, or is tolerant in receiving medicines.
But if he is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and mastications cleansing the brain are administered beforehand for many days with improvement of diet.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner: and with another cautery in his occiput, and above every horn of his head with a cautery. But if the patient is strong and is tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned in the case of one having paralysis, and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner which preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then apply a thin cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in melancholia.
When the cause of melancholia is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we mentioned in the case of one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholia is an excess inclined toward melancholia, and the body of the infirm is moist, then give him something to drink which will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division; then shave the head of the infirm, and afterward make a properly made compress of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head; and the infirm person sitting squarely should be held on all sides.
Then present the liniment. And it is more worthy from old sheep butter. And heat it over a fire with a temperate measured heat, which a finger can tolerate when inserted into it. Then empty it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this for the patient once every week, with his other good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making very small points of it, except that you hold your hand with the cautery: rather let it be by smelling.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with a quality.
Then place on it a piece of cloth soaked in butter or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the water descending to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is shown to you by the signs which I have mentioned in the division, then begin and purge the patient with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all dampness, and make him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then order him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him on the two temples with two cauteries, if the beginning of the descent of water is in both eyes at once; or on one side, if the beginning of water is in one eye: and cut off with the cautery all the veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples: and beware of a flow of blood.
If you see anything of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting off of them, and caution from a flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries ultimately produced.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old, constant, and are upon the veins and arteries which are in the exterior of the head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the same cautery that I narrated in the beginning of descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries upon the two temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the two bones. And if you need addition, then cauterize it on every side cautiously of the eye, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in nasal stench.
When you treat it with what we said in the division, and the medication does not help: then hasten, and give the patient  infirmocochias to drink for three nights; then shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an olive-shaped cautery. Then cauterize it with a nail-shaped cautery, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the nail-shaped cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in each part; and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not move your hand with the cautery too much, but according to the amount that burns a third of the eyelid.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are inverted, stinging the eye.
Cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with fire, or cauterization with a burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, however, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who cleanse them, until they are lengthened and made even. But if they prick him at their root, then bind his eyes with a bandage, so that they do not move, until they grow.
When therefore they grow and are even, then place the patient's head in your bosom; then mark upon the eyelid of his eyes with a cautery, a mark which is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a pledget soaked in egg white or in psyllium mucilage upon the eye.
Then heat the cautery, whose form is this.
Then cauterize over the shape which you marked, little by little in many times, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, the whole appearing properly.
And a sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye now contract, and the hairs rise up at the puncture of the eye.
Then raise your hand and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a pledget with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
But if some of the hairs return after a time, and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cautery on that place, as you did at first.
But if the hairs are below, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place and is level so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is to instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even. Make from paper or cloth a shape like a myrtle leaf.
Then take of known soap and of unslaked lime, one ounce of each or thereabouts; then grind them together well and quickly, so that it does not get cold. Then spread some of it on the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on one or both eyelids. And place under the eye a piece of cotton soaked in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it gently. And you should move it whenever the patient feels the medicine biting; for its bite is like fire.
While, therefore, the biting sensation persists, then remove the medicine and move it with your finger. When, therefore, the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rising, as it rises with burning or with incision, it is well: and if not, then apply more medicine to the place where the medicine does not impress and does not blacken, until your operation is even, and the eye is contracted.
Then place a pledget with butter on it until the burnt skin is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphnic ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you in the operation that you observe the utmost care, lest anything of the medicine fall into the eye.
But if the eyelid softens afterwards, and something fights from the hairs in the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which softens from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who studies this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a lachrymal fistula.
When you treat a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your bosom, and let a servant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it is not moved or shaken.
Then place a cotton pledget soaked in egg white or in flaxseed mucilage over his eye; then heat the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's quill from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish it to be penetrating to the other end, and if you wish it to be upward, try it thus.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then squeeze the fistula, if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it, and draw out its pus.
Then apply the cautery, which is made very hot, to it.
And hold your hand with it a little near the cautery from the eye, toward the side of the nose, so that your hand may not err, or the patient be disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and destroy it.
Therefore, if you reach the bone with the beginning of your cautery, it will be good. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then apply a pledget with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
But if forty days have passed, and it is not healed, then put a sharp corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the ancients mentioned. Direct yourself to the place of the fistula, and incise it; then place in the incision a thin tube, that is, a thin cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of molten lead, and hold your hand with good retention of the cannula, and let the patient not move at all, so that the molten lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the eye of the patient a compress soaked in egg white or in water.
For the lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said, by cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer to the opening of the nose, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come in its own place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing fissures of the lips.
Fissures, which are called chaps, often occur on the lip, and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures with what we have said in the division of illnesses, and the treatment does not help, then cauterize with a small, knife-shaped cautery iron, according to this form.
And let its concavity be according to the thinness of a knife.
Then quickly apply the heated iron to the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerate until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an oral fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, then it forms pus and bursts; afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to apply a heated cautery according to the size it occupies in the fistula. Then insert the heated instrument into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said concerning treatment until it is cured.
If therefore the pus is cut away and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come into its head.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened because of humors, and the teeth are loose, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the patient's head in your lap.
Then a cautery of fire, whose form will come later, so that you place a cannula on the tooth: and quickly insert the heated cautery into it: and hold your hand for a little while, until the patient feels the heat of the fire has now reached the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, as you wish.
Then let the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the loose tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt humor is dried.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for toothache.
When the toothache is due to coldness, or there is cold or a worm in the tooth, and treatment with medicines is ineffective: then cauterization is indicated in two ways: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
Now cauterization with butter is performed by taking cow's butter and melting it in an iron spoon or in a small pan. Then take a small piece of cotton and wrap it around the end of a probe. Then dip it into the melted butter and quickly place it on the aching tooth and hold it until it cools; then repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cotton into cold butter and place it on the aching tooth; then place a hot iron on top of it until the heat penetrates to the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Cauterization with fire is done by using a bronze or iron tube. And let there be something of thickness in its body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery, whatever shape it may be, and place it on that tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either that same day or another.
And it is necessary in the impression of that cautery that the patient fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for an hour; then he should spit it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish, as far as possible; and this is the shape of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in strumae.
When strumae are from phlegm and cold humors, and are not amenable to digestion by medicines, and you wish to digest them quickly: then a concave cautery of fire, whose shape is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may escape from the cautery from one end: and place it, ignited, upon the abscess once, and a second time if it is needed, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
But if the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it lint infused in butter until what the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment until it heals in the shape of a tube.
Concerning the method of cauterization in hoarseness of the voice and shortness of breath.
When humors overcome the lung passage, and especially when it is with coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be evacuated first with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the uvula near the root of the throat in a depressed place: and beware lest you reach the throat with the cautery, nor the skin, except a little of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the joint of the neck at the last vertebra, finishing it: and let the cautery be nail-shaped according to the method which preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in illnesses of the lung and cough.
When cough and illness of the lung are from cold humors, and the infirm person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the illness is of long standing: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, soft, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be a cannula according to the form which preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, which is called a Point, whose form preceded in the puncturing of earache: and let the points be from thirty points up to about others.
Then treat him with what preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore the cauterization is alleviated with it, when you do with it at once three cauterizations.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated because of humors, and it is not fixed at the time of its return from its dislocation, until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated by a small movement, which happens as we have already testified, then it is necessary that you reduce the dislocation in the first place. Then let the patient be laid on his back, or on his sound side. Then raise the skin which is in the inner armpit upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then have a cautery with two prongs. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauterizations.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, wherefore the figure of the cauterization then becomes six cauterizations: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the probe.
And this is the form of a cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added in this way, wherefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt on the cautery. Then make the patient adhere to stillness, so that the limb is not moved for some time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is towards the upper parts, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed: and the patient is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When coldness and much moisture occur in the stomach, until they draw it away from its complexion, and catarrhs are multiplied to it, and continuous methods of treatment do not help: then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and that he extend his legs and his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the breastbone the size of one finger with a nail-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below on the two sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And lengthen the distance between them so that they do not join, when they produce pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery with which this is done be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by puncturing it for him who is frightened by this cautery: and it is so that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity which you wish with a cautery: then cauterize it with a pointed cautery: then treat it with the treatment which preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver from coldness and dampness, or from gross flatulence, until it departs from its natural complexion by superfluous evacuation, and the sick person is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid supine on his neck, and you mark with a cautery three cauterizations according to this figure, and this same quantity on the lower liver from the hypochondria, where the elbow of a man reaches: and let the space which is between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of a straight body: and do not press your hand with the cautery very much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, half that quantity not added: and let the sick person be standing on his feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him be lying down, who now extends his legs and raises his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And indeed it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizations with a knife-cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed too deeply in the cauterization, and burn the whole thickness of the skin, wherefore the whole body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: because the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
Concerning the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When an exit wound occurs, and you wish to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its membrane: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person suffers pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the membrane of the liver, there is intense sharp pain; and you see now that its treatment has wearied the physicians.
Therefore, the patient must lie on his back. Then mark the location of the abscess with a cautery; then heat a cautery that resembles a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the whole skin is burned, and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this type of cautery, except for one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands these illnesses occur with some experience: then indeed let him dare to perform such an operation.
But truly, to leave it, is better for me.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said, cautery with the roots of birthwort for cold pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you should receive of the long dried roots of birthwort, one longer root, which is found among them, and let it be like the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil: and ignite it in the fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the clavicle with the neck, and with two small cauteries somewhat obliquely below the chin towards the part which is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib somewhat obliquely towards the back: and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades: and with two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, lower than the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary that you compress your hand with the cautery, rather let it be evident on the skin by smelling.
And now some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron similar to a ray: and they ignite it, and internally insert it into that which is between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess with it, and pus comes out: as we said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear that either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no healing.
Chapter XXXII. On the method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with that which we have said of treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then cautery is used in it according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One of which is that you make three cauteries, or four, in a line according to the length of the spleen, according to the figure of the cauteries of the liver, whose figure preceded.
And let there be between each cautery the amount of the thickness of a finger, or a little more.
And let the method of cautery be, as we said in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you ignite a cautery having two prongs, which we spoke of in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus: and lift the skin which is in line with the spleen, where the patient's left elbow reaches: and let your lifting of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two very hot prongs until you penetrate the skin with them on the other side: then withdraw the cautery: therefore four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then take care of the cautery after you let it go, that it discharges pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than the other things which preceded from the treatment.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
Cautery does not fall in dropsy, except for ascites properly.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment which we mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery above the stomach, and another cautery above the liver, and a cautery above the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one in the direction of the chest, and another in the direction of the stomach: and let the quantity of the depth of the cautery be near the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it emits pus for a long time.
And do not remove the patient from treatment after cautery with it: for it is necessary that two intentions are combined for him; and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form, however, of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized, is nail-shaped: according to what preceded its form; and that with which the back is cauterized, is olive-shaped according to what preceded its form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses form in a dropsical patient and are filled with yellowish water, it is necessary to cauterize on the dorsum of the foot in the space which is between the little and ring fingers; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand; and do not repeat it at all.
Then the yellowish water will sweat out, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make two cauteries on each of the two legs, and let the cautery be made with the knife-like end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another lower than that, about the middle of the leg; and on each hip two cauteries; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may sweat out from it; then treat it with the other things which we have mentioned.
Concerning the method of cauterization in looseness of the bowels.
Chapter 35.
When there is looseness of the bowels from cold and humors, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of treatment, and is not healed; and you see the patient tolerating cauterization of exuberant virtue, then cauterize him with a large cautery over his stomach, as preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and with four small cauteries around the navel, with a thin nail-like cautery; and with a large cautery over the alcatin above the alhosos, or with two cauteries.
And if you see exuberant humors, and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery over the pubis, and with a cautery over each ilium; and perhaps you will add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupt humors, and they are treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries above the lower vertebra of the back under the almeidati somewhat triangularly, and with a cautery below the navel as if by two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming inflamed, then cauterize him above the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded: and cauterize above his liver, and another above his spleen, with a nail-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him, until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut away althelul, then heat a cautery that resembles a ray. Then insert it, heated, into the excised althelul: and  move your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with what benefits them of ointments until they heal.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the alcatin, it is more ultimate in aid.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the patient does not submit to the incision and the operation which we have described in its place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he may be cured with a cautery.
Therefore, when a fistula occurs in someone, and it becomes old, pus and corrupt humors flow from it. It is therefore more fitting that you should probe it with a slender probe. Then ascertain the amount of its depth with a probe.
Then heat a cautery which is similar to a ray. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula and the amount that the nail entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to your need.
And guard yourself from burning a nerve, if it is there, or a large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all those places.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed, and the materials are cut away from it, and it remains so for a long time: then know that it is now completely healed.
And if materials are not cut away from it, then know that it is penetrating, or a rotten bone is in its depth, or something like that from those things: the mention of which will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from gross flatulence, and the patient’s strength is diminished because of it, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the almethen on the kidneys themselves, cauterizing each kidney with a cautery iron, the mention of which has preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time in the almeidatu itself. Therefore three lines will result. Therefore the last will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder from cold and moisture, until the patient does not retain urine, then cauterize it in the lower part of the pubis above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubis begin, and cauterize from the right side of the pubis, and another from the left: and let the length of that lateral cauterization be according to the size of the thumb's knuckle; and cauterize it with a cautery of the lower back, or two cauteries, if you need it: and let it be according to the preceding cautery of the nail.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, and it is prevented by that from impregnation, and her menses are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain happens to her at their arrival, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above the pubis on the lower back, or two cauteries; and let the cautery be nail-shaped.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors are poured out to the socket of the hip, and they become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg is longer than the other, when they are compared together; and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the patient above the socket of his hip with a cautery similar to a circle: after you mark with a hot iron around the socket, as it is rotated: and so that the socket itself falls in the middle of the circle.
But if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-shaped cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the amount of the thickness of all the skin.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness, and the patient is treated with what we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic, then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is, that you cauterize above the hip joint itself with three triangular cauterizations, according to this form. And make them a good, or bad, depth. And let the space that is between each cauterization be the amount of the thickness of a finger: and let the cauterization be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, a cauterization is done in the middle on the head of the hip joint itself. Therefore there are four cauterizations.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, which preceded in form in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, with one: so that it is a circle containing the whole hip.
And burn the thickness of the whole skin.
This is the method of cauterization in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the thigh, above the place to which the sick person points there, in which there is pain, and with your cautery above the ankle with four fingers to the outside a little: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
But if the sick person indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize it there where he points with a pointed cautery, with three, or four, or more, if it needs it.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And beware in all your cauterization, lest you reach with the cautery so as to burn a nerve, or a large artery, and draw through that upon the sick person a serious harm, or contraction.
And I indeed have already seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the ankle, and went too far in cauterization, and the leg swelled, until the swelling reached the foot, and it was wholly perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then there followed a breaking of the belly, and death after that.
But if the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said concerning the cauterization of the hip, of which this is the method of cautery. Make a similar tube of iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date-stone, or somewhat less: and within that tube let there be a third tube.
And let the space which is between each tube be the amount of a thumb-joint: and let the tubes be open on two sides: and let their height be about a joint, or two joints: and make for them a handle of iron decently fitted to the tubes.
Then let it be heated in the fire until it glows red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed upon the hip-socket, the patient lying on his healthy side. Cauterize him therefore with three round cauteries at once.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, "With this kind of cautery, O my sons, we have used it little, because of the terror of its appearance: and therefore, because we have found few who would endure it.
Nevertheless, it is among the good cauteries for him who endures it, and finds with it its place.
Now the cautery with burning medicines is such that you make two samia having a perforated ring, into which descends a hinge of its door made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall: on whose height there are two nodes, or something like them.
And let the space which is between both be the quantity of the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let that which they contain be joined together, according to this form.
Then place it over the hip socket, the patient lying on the healthy side. And press your hand very much upon the hip socket. Then pour between the two circles some warm water, which has been heated a little with fire, and hold it for the amount of an hour: and let the patient endure its biting and its burning, for he finds the biting like fire, until the biting ceases.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe away the warm water from the whole hip with fresh water: then leave it for three days.
And put butter on it, until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for some days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the ultimate in aid.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the pain extends to the hip or leg: make him sit in what contains water, as you did with the hip equally.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, one part of each; grind both, and put them in a new pot, the lower part of which is perforated with one small hole, according to the size that the ray may enter; and put under the bottom of the pot another glass pot; and pour over the alkali and lime fresh water, which submerges both by a finger’s breadth; after which you compress them with your hand with good compression; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over more lime; and filter until it is renewed.
For then it will be of very strong sharpness, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other members. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And among medicines are those with which ankles are cauterized, also such as tesisie, and cashew nut oil, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed.
And Galen indeed, in narrating, recounted the cure of a certain man from antiquity, by which he was cured of hip pain and sciatica; and he magnified it to be very great. And he said that he did not need another cure, and that he was healed in a single time, until he recounted that he perhaps entered the bath carried, and came out of it already healed.
And it is so that it is taken from green seitaragi; and if green is not found, let dry, fresh be taken; and let it be ground much with some fat, and let it be placed upon the hip, where there is pain, or leg, or in the thigh; and let it be bound, and let it be left for the quantity of three hours, or for the quantity that the infirm person feels a lessening of the burning. Then introduce him into the bath.
Therefore, when his body becomes moist, introduce him into the bath. For the pain recedes, and it is healed.
And know that it is not necessary that anyone use a cautery with these medicines, except after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides also said that goat dung, when the sciatic vein is cauterized with it, benefits it: and the cautery is done in this way. Let wool be taken, and let it be soaked in old oil, and let it be placed upon the deep place which is between the thumb of the foot and the ankle, and is closer to the ankle.
Then take dry goat dung, and burn it in the fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease doing this until feeling comes to the middle as far as the ankle, and the pain rests.
And this method of cautery is called vaccinum cautery.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist material: and indeed cautery is not appropriate except in this type alone, which results from the infusion of cold material.
Therefore, after evacuating the patient with foul-smelling pills and the like, three lines should be made on the back where the pain is, according to the width of the patient’s almeida, after marking with encausto five cauteries in each line, or more according to the amount that the patient’s tolerance and strength allow: and the cauterization should be done with a punctate cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, with a medial nail cautery, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the beginning of humpback.
This illness often happens to small infants.
And the sign of its beginning in boys is that a constriction occurs in their breathing upon elevation and movement; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and its knots that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see this and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular in this form.
And let the cautery take equally upon every part of the vertebra; and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a pointed cautery in two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware lest you apply the cautery to the hump which occurs in a spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in gout and the pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors which are poured out into any limbs of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is the custom of physicians to name this properly gout.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of healing and the pains are not removed, then cautery removes them.
And it is so that he cauterizes it after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to puncture on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. But if the pains ascend to the knees, or the remaining joints, and this happens many times, then cauterize it above each knee with three cauteries, or four on every side, with this same nail-shaped cautery.
If, however, more are necessary to you with this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, but rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and the back: then administer what we said of the cautery in its chapter.
But if the pains are in the hands only, then puncture around the wrists, as two lines are rolled around.
But if pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them, above every node a puncture, and above the ridge of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not deprive the patient of good regimen, of the reception of medicines. For if good regimen is done, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with God's help with this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine or bladder descends to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary that you order the patient to omit eating on his day. And that he use emollients, so that stool descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back; and instruct him to hold his breath, until the bladder or intestine emerges or appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cautery under the rupture on the pubic bone, with a mark whose end is similar to half a circle towards the upper parts of the body.
Then heat the cautery, which is of this form, until it becomes white and throws off sparks. Then return the intestine or bladder to its cavity. Then let the assistant place his hand on the place, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the legs of the patient, and placed a cushion under him, and another servant over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark, your hand with the cautery standing straight. And hold it until you reach the bone with it; or repeat with it another time, if you have not reached the bone with it in the first attempt.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and there comes upon the patient through it either death or great harm.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your operation is not effective.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be slender, according to their size.
Then treat with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you give him nourishment for the length of time of his cure, which softens his bowels, so that the intestine does not come out during straining and evacuation.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then apply a properly made bandage, and let him keep it on for another forty days.
And let him be lessened from labor, and from repletion of food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus he is healed with a complete healing.
And I will describe the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen, and are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be then as a third of it. Then treat him with what we have said: and it will not increase.
And now some early authors have said: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a branding iron, and a line is placed which is across the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a nail-cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterization in pains due to a fall or blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some member from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of every member be according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it heals from the first cauterization, it is well. If not, then repeat the cauterization on it.
For it is customary for these pains to move from one member to that which is near it. Therefore it is necessary that you pursue them with cautery, until the sick person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
Lepers, however, are sometimes helped by cautery with the greatest benefit. And especially the type of leprosy which occurs because of the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore when you wish to cauterize it, consider.
Therefore if the leprosy is incipient, and you have treated it with what we have said in the division, and it does not subside, nor remain static: and you fear for the patient, that corruption will spread over his whole constitution: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, markedly, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And lastly, apply your hand with the cautery lightly, until it imprints a small mark on the skin, and the crusts are loosened from it: so that the exhalation of thick vapors from it may be relieved, and cauterize also with a cautery over the spleen itself, as has preceded.
But if the leprosy is already spread over the patient, and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries which we have mentioned on the head, and a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the two cheekbones, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the al-hahos [? - unclear word in original] near the coccyx and one above it, in the almeidati [? - unclear word in original]: and two on the hips: namely one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the soft parts of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, of the joints of his fingers, and toes: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the wrists of his hands.
And beware of the nerves which are on the back of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the pubic bone, and another on the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you add cauterization, the more it is helpful, and the more it contributes.
And know that the patient does not find pain in cauterization, as healthy people find it: because his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what preceded in the types of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with herb flour with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in numbness.
When a limb is numb, and it is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterize that numb limb with cauteries, according to what the size or smallness of the limb deserves.
And let your cautery penetrate a little into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes something causing numbness, which happens to the hand and foot, is cauterized in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves which move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
Truly, let no one presume to do this except one who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter 51.
When the albaras is of long standing and nothing from the arts of medicine benefits it, then cauterize it superficially with a deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with herb flour, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and pigeon's blood, and swallow's blood: of each let there be one part; let these all be mixed, and spread on a cloth, and applied to the place, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a cancer.
When a cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it is rolled.
The wise, however, have said that it should be cauterized with a final cautery in the middle.
But to me that does not seem good; because I fear that it will ulcerate; and I have already seen that happen several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Adultery.
When someone has an abscess, and it is slow in maturing, either because of the superfluity producing it, or because of the patient's age, when he is decrepit and has little blood, or because of the time, and one wishes to hasten the maturation of the abscess, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, puncturing. Then leave it. For it itself will hasten with maturation.
But if you wish its perforation with a cautery, then a fire cautery, whose form is this.
And place it in the middle of the abscess, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which follows the infirmity, so that the flow of pus may be alleviated.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a corroding ulcer.
Chapter 54.
A corroding ulcer is nothing but a corruption in a limb that moves about and corrodes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore if you see a corroding ulcer in a place which can tolerate cauterization with fire, then have many fire cauteries, small and large nails, according to what is suitable for the place in which the corroding ulcer is.
Then cauterize it on every side until you eradicate the whole corruption, and nothing at all of it remains.
Then leave it for three days, and apply crushed sulfur with oil to the cauterized areas until all the eschars and all the corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
Therefore if you see that after three days flesh grows in a healthy growth, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
And a corrosive is sometimes medicated with a sharp medicine. For it arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker help: and I indeed have already spoken of its cauterization with a sharp medicine in the division: therefore accept it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Clavus and Verrucae.
Chapter 55.
This ailment often happens in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a coarse, hardened thing which harms the foot.
And cautery in them is according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for that with fire, make a concave iron cautery similar to a vulture's feather:  made of iron, according to the size which contains the clavus on all sides; and let it have thin edges.
Then place it, heated, upon the clavus. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the clavus, until the cautery reaches the depth of the clavus: and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then plaster it with wild mallows, crushed with salt: and leave the plaster on it at night. Then it itself will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the place with an ointment generating flesh, until it is healed.
